<div id="review_311655061" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/311655061" />
    <a title="Lisbeth Avery {Domus Libri}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8282085-lisbeth-avery-domus-libri"><img alt="Lisbeth Avery {Domus Libri}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426613564p2/8282085.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/311655061?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisbeth Avery {Domus Libri}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisbeth Avery {Domus Libri}" href="/user/show/8282085-lisbeth-avery-domus-libri">Lisbeth Avery {Domus Libri}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8282085-lisbeth-avery-domus-libri?shelf=one-star">one-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8282085-lisbeth-avery-domus-libri?shelf=high-expectations">high-expectations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8282085-lisbeth-avery-domus-libri?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8282085-lisbeth-avery-domus-libri?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8282085-lisbeth-avery-domus-libri?shelf=disappointed">disappointed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8282085-lisbeth-avery-domus-libri?shelf=dnf-review">dnf-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer311655061" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16433710198838952870"><b>DNF Review</b><br/><br/>Slated is one of those books that sound great in theory but in actuality, it didn't end up that great. Reading the blurb made me extremely excited but the book however is the exact opposite. While there were many flaws to the novel, the major one was the fact that the book was written in the first person.<br/><br/>To understand why this was a monumental fail on the author's part, you need to know something about the main character. Thankfully, this won't be a very long interruption because there</span>
  <span id="freeText16433710198838952870" style="display:none"><b>DNF Review</b><br /><br />Slated is one of those books that sound great in theory but in actuality, it didn't end up that great. Reading the blurb made me extremely excited but the book however is the exact opposite. While there were many flaws to the novel, the major one was the fact that the book was written in the first person.<br /><br />To understand why this was a monumental fail on the author's part, you need to know something about the main character. Thankfully, this won't be a very long interruption because there isn't much to say about her.<br /><br />Kyla is the main character who's traumatic backstory includes brain wash and stuff. Yeah, poor baby, .ect. Someone however forgot to tell Kyla that brainwash does not mean you become akin to say a robot or a door.<br /><br />Actually no, there are robots and doors with more energy and vigour than her. She's worse. <br /><br />Kyla is seriously the most colorless, commonplace, dead, drab, drudging, dull, flat, ho hum, humdrum, insipid, interminable, irksome, lifeless, monotonous, moth-eaten, mundane, nothing, nowhere, platitudinous, plebeian, prosaic, repetitious, routine, spiritless, stale, stereotyped, stodgy, stuffy, stupid, tame, tedious, threadbare, tiresome, tiring, trite, unexciting, uninteresting, unvaried, vapid, wearisome (no I did not just copy the thesaurus entry for boring... heh) character out there. <br /><br />Consequently, the writing is the driest monotone out there and there is pretty much absolutely nothing to keep you going. Like, how am I supposed to stay <s>awake</s> interested when much of the book sounds like this:<br /><br /><blockquote>‘Interesting choice for breakfast,’ Amy says, then sits up and yawns. ‘Are you an early bird?’<br />I look at her blankly.<br />‘Do you always wake up early?’<br />I consider. ‘I think so,’ I say, finally. ‘Though that could be because at the hospital you have no choice.’<br />‘Oh, I remember that. Horrible morning buzzer. Breakfast by six.’ She shudders.<br />‘Want one?’ I hold out the box.<br />‘Oooh, tempting. Maybe later, when I’m more awake. What is that?’ She points at the folder in my other hand.<br />‘My drawings.’<br />‘Can I see?’<br />I hesitate. I rarely show them to anyone, though Dr Lysander insisted on checking through them now and then.<br />‘You don’t have to show me if you don’t want to.’<br />I sit next to her and open the folder, pull out the sheets of paper. Amy exclaims at the one on top. A self-portrait. Me, but different: half as I am in the mirror, the other half skin missing, eyeball hanging from an empty socket.<br />‘May I?’ she holds out a hand, and I pass the drawing to her.<br />But that wasn’t on top before. I start flipping through the sheets.<br />‘You’re so good, this is amazing.’</blockquote><br />This is an actual conversation from the book, by the way. This is actually how she sounds throughout the book.<br /><br />Not even the plot could keep me going because honestly, it's extremely flat and boring. There isn't enough to really keep the story moving because all and any plot twists were easily guessed.<br /><br />The author gives away all the clues in such a way that it becomes incredibly obvious. While sometimes hiding things in plain sight is great, it doesn't always work. Especially when you have little to no skill. World building is what readers look for and they remember it. If you put a crucial bit of information right in front of their eyes, they'll see it.<br /><br />The whole cast of characters were bland, to put it lightly. They had little to no personality or distinguishing characteristics. Everyone talked in the same monotone as Kyla, except for one of the characters who had the bubbly manic pixie personality which is less of a personality and more of a stereotype, if you get what I mean.<br /><br />So, the boring plot/characters and terrible writing joined forces to create one of the most dull stories I have ever read. I would not recommend this book to anyone and would advise you all to stay approximately 50 feet away at all times.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16433710198838952870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_515592471" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/515592471" />
    <a title="Katy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4572741-katy"><img alt="Katy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365039295p2/4572741.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/515592471?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katy" href="/user/show/4572741-katy">Katy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399161728" href="/book/show/15812184-slated">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer515592471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer253857325895014269">2.5 stars - Gah! I don't know how to rate this one! On one hand, it FELT long, and I was SO bored for the first 2/3 of the book. And the last 1/3 was VERY exciting, but I'm left feeling like I didn't learn anything after finishing the book.<br/><br/>The first part of the book was really dull. I understand that Terry was trying to put us in the mindset that Kyla had to relearn everything, but honestly, it did NOTHING for story. What's the significance of her learning how to open the car door or doing the d</span>
  <span id="freeText253857325895014269" style="display:none">2.5 stars - Gah! I don't know how to rate this one! On one hand, it FELT long, and I was SO bored for the first 2/3 of the book. And the last 1/3 was VERY exciting, but I'm left feeling like I didn't learn anything after finishing the book.<br /><br />The first part of the book was really dull. I understand that Terry was trying to put us in the mindset that Kyla had to relearn everything, but honestly, it did NOTHING for story. What's the significance of her learning how to open the car door or doing the dishes and cutting her hand with a knife? And I'd understand if i was just a few examples before moving along with the story, but Terry spent about half the book telling us about Kyla's relearning experiences, and none of those contributed to the story development.<br /><br />I would have been more interested if Terry had spent that time world-building. It took me a while to figure out that this was in the future, way past 2030 (the year Mum was in her teens?), and I get that there's a normal wold and the hospital, but that's about it. MUCH later, Mum tells us a little bit about the political campaign that kind of brought everything on, but it was very brief and didn't tell us much.<br /><br />While I knew from the prologue and the nightmares that those things had something to do with why she was different, it doesn't give me much to go on. I guess that she built a wall to protect herself, but that's about it. Why did she like to draw? Why wouldn't anyone let her take art? Why all of a sudden they let her draw? Why were some of her artwork taken away? Why did she have to hide some of them? And why is it bad to be left handed? All of these questions. Nothing was answered.<br /><br />And I still haven't decided whether I like Ben or not. He's an okay character, but not one that make you immediately like him. And I couldn't tell whether he was a good guy that became enlightened when he met her or if he was there to trick her all along. I guess it was the way the romance was written. It was shoddy, at best, which makes me not want to trust him. There's just something off about the whole thing, and I think a lot of it was the way Ben's character was written and how disconnected I felt to him.<br /><br />The problem is, I still don't see a clear line of who all the parties are. I mean, I know there are the Lorders and the AGT, and of course you're going to wonder who really are the good guys and the bad guys. But I can't tell which side Mum and Dad are on - nor can I really tell if they're even on the same side. I think there is a lot more to Dr. Lysander, and even though I had Ms. Ali, I can't tell which side she is on. And what is the deal with Wayne Best? It can't be pure coincidence that he targets Kyla instead of Amy or another Slater, and I know he is Phoebe's uncle, but he's not just a random creepy guy.<br /><br />So overall, I think the premise is great. I just think it took way too long to get into the story - without good reason - and I think once I was in the story, I had more questions than I got answers. By the end of the book, I'm left knowing what happened but bursting with more uncertainty. I know Terry is planning to leave some of that for book 2, but I just feel like the hours I just spent on a book that FELT long, I was just hoping I would have had more answers.<br /><br />Having said that, I AM dying to know what happens next - mostly because I want answers, damnit! I'm sure Terry is saving all the good stuff for the next book, so they better be good answers because I have high expectations now. The sequel better blow me away.</span>
  <a data-text-id="253857325895014269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_627432279" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/627432279" />
    <a title="Ellie Red" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12422704-ellie-red"><img alt="Ellie Red" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419437952p2/12422704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer11253278534320711791">M-I-N-D-B-L-O-W-I-N-G!!!!!!!!!!!!!<br/>Five stars are simply not enough! Slated is one of those books that you are so happy you bought, it is worth every single euro! Slated is about a girl that her memories have been wiped but she feels something is wrong and different about her. Set in a village near London in 2055 (I think). It is brilliant, full of twists and suspense! It is very cinematographic. It is genius, everything in this novel can be explained in a logical manner that makes sense, nothing</span>
  <span id="freeText11253278534320711791" style="display:none">M-I-N-D-B-L-O-W-I-N-G!!!!!!!!!!!!!<br />Five stars are simply not enough! Slated is one of those books that you are so happy you bought, it is worth every single euro! Slated is about a girl that her memories have been wiped but she feels something is wrong and different about her. Set in a village near London in 2055 (I think). It is brilliant, full of twists and suspense! It is very cinematographic. It is genius, everything in this novel can be explained in a logical manner that makes sense, nothing is just out there. Also it has a little bit of romance, it doesn't dominate the story which is a good thing. All in all a wonderful novel which you don't want to miss!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_278487037" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/278487037" />
    <a title="Misty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1124284-misty"><img alt="Misty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539720622p2/1124284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/278487037?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Misty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Misty" href="/user/show/1124284-misty">Misty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=dystopia-postapocalyptic">dystopia-postapocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=juvenile-ya">juvenile-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=arc-or-galley">arc-or-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=sci_fi-fantasy">sci_fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=review-copy-accepted">review-copy-accepted</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer278487037" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10825565412828837959">With dystopian books being as popular as they are right now, it always makes me a little wary when I pick one up. I mean, I love them, don't get me wrong. But it's inevitable when you have a lot of something that they each get a little farther from the core of what makes that something good. Each dystopia seems to be a little...fluffier than the last, and a little more farfetched. To me, you can see the <i>truth</i> in a good dystopia. As bizarre as the society portrayed may be, some little part of you</span>
  <span id="freeText10825565412828837959" style="display:none">With dystopian books being as popular as they are right now, it always makes me a little wary when I pick one up. I mean, I love them, don't get me wrong. But it's inevitable when you have a lot of something that they each get a little farther from the core of what makes that something good. Each dystopia seems to be a little...fluffier than the last, and a little more farfetched. To me, you can see the <i>truth</i> in a good dystopia. As bizarre as the society portrayed may be, some little part of you is made <u>extremely</u> uncomfortable while reading it because it feels like it could maybe happen. Dystopias hold up a mirror to some aspect of our society, and then project that aspect to its logical extreme.<br /><br />While <i>Slated</i> may occasionally fall into some of the fluffy-dystopia traps (not <i>every</i> book needs a romance, dammit!), it generally wiggles itself right back out of those traps, and more importantly, touches on what makes dystopia dystopia - it feels like it could happen.<br /><br />The idea of Slating, of a forced mind-wipe, is intriguing because it's something I could <i>easily</i> see being researched in a lab somewhere <b>right now</b>. I mean, it's reprogramming, essentially, and <i>we already do that</i> in one form or another. But what makes it so eerie, what makes it seem so plausible, is the idea of it being presented as something altruistic and just - the best, boldest, kindest solution to a problem. Why lock criminals away and let them rot? What good is that doing? What if instead we could simply <i>remake</i> them? What if we could reach into their brains, give their memory Etch-a-Sketch a little shake, and begin anew? And as a failsafe, we'll just have this little brain monitor that would zap the hell out of you if you tried to hurt someone - and maybe even if you get too sad...Wouldn't <i>everyone</i> be better off then? The criminals would get a chance to be productive and happy, and the criminalized would get to feel safe again. Problem solved.<br />See how easy it is to justify something like this? I guarantee there are people in our society now who would absolutely see the benefits in this and would even promote the science.<br /><br />That is, if it weren't for one little thing: abuses. Because let's be honest, there's NO WAY this wouldn't be abused. And there you have it: the crux of dystopia. How far can you go before the potential good is outweighed by the potential bad? Terry walked this line really well and as the book went on, was clearly able to convey the snowball effect something like this would have, and the way this kind of legislature/propaganda would creep up on the general public until they find themselves having agreed to a totalitarian society with no real recourse to change things <i>back</i>.<br /><br />But getting beyond the dystopian aspect, the book is just thoroughly readable. It's engaging right from the start, and Kyla is an intriguing main character. She's fascinating because she doesn't know who she is now or who she was before, but she lives in fear of her unknown past - what must she have done to be slated? The reader is right there with her, wondering if Kyla was part of a terrorist organization, wondering if she was an abused child who turned the tables - wondering what could possible have gotten this bright, artistic, seemingly sweet child slated. As a character with no past, she could have seemed substance-less, but she didn't at all. In fact, she is a sharp counterpoint to many of the other slateds around her, and she only becomes more complex and intriguing (and even more mysterious) as the story goes on.<br /><br />Now, as I mentioned above, there is a romance, and frankly I could have done with out it. But that's because I'm heartless. I think it was actually pretty well handled (for the most part) and didn't seem forced on the story for the sake of having the Obligatory YA Romance. And there was one thing that happened in the end that redeemed the story-as-far-as-romance-goes for me, and it's spoilery so I'm not going to tell you what, but when you read it you're going to say, <i>Man, she wasn't kidding about being heartless...</i><br /><i>
  <br />
</i><br />And that's all I'm going to say, other than this: When I started this, I stayed up very late into the night and read the first 100+ pages in one sitting. But this was just before Fairy Tale Fortnight, so I really <i>had</i> to put it down, because frankly I should never have picked it up yet. I didn't <i>mean</i> to read the first 100+ pages, I just wanted to get a feel for the story. Putting it down and not coming back to it for almost a month could have <b>really</b> backfired. Sometimes a story grips you in the beginning and you read it voraciously and <u>LOVE IT</u> at the time, and then once you've had some breathing room, you're like, What exactly did I like about that again? It's book crack, and though you love it initially, you regret it later. Putting this down could have revealed this as book crack, if it wasn't a good story. But when I came back to it, I was <i>right back in it</i> like I'd never left. It engulfed me again, and when I was finished, all I could think was how <i>l o n g</i> the wait was going to be until the next book.<br />So. Long.<br /><br />So now I need you to read it so we can commiserate. ;D</span>
  <a data-text-id="10825565412828837959" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3107235878" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3107235878" />
    <a title="Audrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5630113-audrey"><img alt="Audrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572483937p2/5630113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3107235878?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Audrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Audrey" href="/user/show/5630113-audrey">Audrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399161728" href="/book/show/15812184-slated">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5630113-audrey?shelf=2019-books">2019-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5630113-audrey?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3107235878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12089766879100541382"><u>Warning: first person present tense</u><br/><br/>I guess this is dystopia, though the government here doesn’t pretend it’s anything but a police state. The book fulfills the premise well — Kyla has been Slated (had her memories erased) and is ready to be part of a new family and home. She has dreams that are actually memories, which are supposed to be erased, and people around her keep disappearing.<br/><br/>There HAS to be a love interesting, obviously. I wish a guy and a girl, especially young teens, could be just go</span>
  <span id="freeText12089766879100541382" style="display:none"><u>Warning: first person present tense</u><br><br>I guess this is dystopia, though the government here doesn’t pretend it’s anything but a police state. The book fulfills the premise well — Kyla has been Slated (had her memories erased) and is ready to be part of a new family and home. She has dreams that are actually memories, which are supposed to be erased, and people around her keep disappearing.<br><br>There HAS to be a love interesting, obviously. I wish a guy and a girl, especially young teens, could be just good friends for once. There is also the wearisome girl-on-girl hate. Every girl automatically hates Kyla when cute boys talk to her. I am so sick of this trope. Kyla herself is a bit of a Mary Sue. All the characters (except girls her age) love her, and she’s pretty near perfect and never makes mistakes.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1577937118ra/28699855.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am also a little confused by the Slating: It is used as a mercy punishment for hardened criminals but can only be done on those under 16. How many mass murderers under 16 can there be? A lot, apparently.<br><br>It was still more interesting than, say, Scythe and many other YA dystopias. It leaves a lot of questions for future books to answer. So not bad if not groundbreaking. The author has a really odd use of punctuation.<br><br>No strong language; no sexual content; some violence<br><br><a href="https://audreytheeditor.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Book Blog</a></span>

<div id="review_381579636" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/381579636" />
    <a title="Richere" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5843318-richere"><img alt="Richere" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332707666p2/5843318.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/381579636?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richere" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richere" href="/user/show/5843318-richere">Richere</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5843318-richere?shelf=1-3-star-ratings">1-3-star-ratings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer381579636&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer381579636" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8441175877772423014">I don't get what's up with all of the 4-5 stars for this book!!! I was DECEIVED by this book. The cover looked absolutely GORGEOUS. The summary absolutely had me believed that I was in for a good long and absolutely exciting and unforgettable read!!<br/><br/>But I was dead wrong.<br/><br/>At first it was slow going and I forced myself to keep reading to see where this went. I should have known from the writing style, the dialogue and how just plain boring the story was, that this was not going to be entertaining in</span>
  <span id="freeText8441175877772423014" style="display:none">I don't get what's up with all of the 4-5 stars for this book!!! I was DECEIVED by this book. The cover looked absolutely GORGEOUS. The summary absolutely had me believed that I was in for a good long and absolutely exciting and unforgettable read!!<br /><br />But I was dead wrong.<br /><br />At first it was slow going and I forced myself to keep reading to see where this went. I should have known from the writing style, the dialogue and how just plain boring the story was, that this was not going to be entertaining in the least; but more like an informative read. I should have recognized the signs of an unsuccessful story sooner to save myself the pain of reading this.<br /><br />First off, our characters don't have memories of who they are, they don't know they're pasts, they don't know their families, and they barely have personalities from who they were before. They're all absolutely robotic. At first I thought that this was understandable; you know, it's the beginning of the story and these robotic actions are bound to change right? Wrong. <br /><br />This is what frustrated me so much!! Yeah although there was a ton of mystery, it was getting to be so boring that the mystery was starting to get annoying -_- Nothing really got anywhere. There was no change. It was always the same locations, same settings, and the same routines. <br /><br />Kyla A.K.A "Lucy" had this constant routine going on in her life with her fake family. God it was boring. The book stayed at the same pace the whole way; Kyla goes to school, goes home, goes to visit the hospital, goes to her group therapy, hangs out with her friend/love interest Ben and then stops, repeats and starts all over again. <br /><br />The repeating sequences BORED. ME. TO. TEARS. And whenever there was the slightest hint of action that was about to happen, nothing happens at all -_- Kyla is a very boring character. I don't know if that's just who she is, or if that was just simply the author's writing style. The same went for all of the other characters, but Kyla was the most boring, and she was our main character for God's sake!!!<br /><br />The summary didn't mention a love interest at all. And when I first read up about Jazz, Amy's boyfriend, I hoped for something to happen between Kyla and him. But I soon realized that, that was not going to happen. Then came Ben; for it to be already 2031 or whatever, I would have thought that at least the NAME would not sound so simple and boring. His name, "Ben" sounded just as boring as his character. It was a pleasant surprise to know that there was some male character involved with our main one, but as far as romance goes, nothing really goes which was really disappointing. All they do is kiss about three times.<br /><br />The whole book felt dry and it dragged. I forced myself to read more, in hopes that at least SOMETHING, would turn up and turn this whole book upside down. I couldn't even finish the last twenty pages or so. I skimmed the rest, and apparently Ben is missing and Kyla is off to find him. <br /><br />I have no interest whatsoever in continuing this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8441175877772423014" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer249355303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer488316538751726724">When I first read this, I agonized because I didn't have book two. Now I have read it again, but this time I am prepared! On to Fractured!<br/><br/>May 9-10, 2014<br/>I think the ending left me with more questions than when I started. The big reveal in the end didn't really fit with what had happened in the earlier pages. I was really drawn into Kayla's world and her story. The idea that we could be remolded into a different human being if our memories were not intact is an interesting premise. It does not all</span>
  <span id="freeText488316538751726724" style="display:none">When I first read this, I agonized because I didn't have book two. Now I have read it again, but this time I am prepared! On to Fractured!<br /><br />May 9-10, 2014<br />I think the ending left me with more questions than when I started. The big reveal in the end didn't really fit with what had happened in the earlier pages. I was really drawn into Kayla's world and her story. The idea that we could be remolded into a different human being if our memories were not intact is an interesting premise. It does not allow for the nature side of the argument. <br /><br />I am quite intrigued by Kayla's new Mum. I think there is so much more there than what we get in the first book. It felt like the entire book was just a set up for the next book. There was no real resolution to any of the problems presented. I am really bummed out that I don't have the next book to read right away. <br /><br />Kayla's artistic talent was a nice touch. My mother-in-law was an amazing artist before her stroke which paralyzed her. She taught herself how to paint with her other hand, and the pieces she painted were just as good. I can see how Kayla could teach herself to draw with her non-dominant hand. <br /><br />I would recommend this to anyone who likes a good dystopian. There are some plot points that you have to suspend belief, but on the whole it was a good solid read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="488316538751726724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

Teri Terry didn't describe things in details. Some parts was left me to judge how. As it has "future-background", I think I'm not the </span>
  <span id="freeText12396745556075241665" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b> IT WAS SUCH AN AMAZING READING EXPERIENCE! </b>
</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422248337ra/13476845.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote> <br><br>This book is terribly terribly well done! I cannot stop reading it. It gave you mystery, thrill, excitement, and many other feeling at once. I was really doubtful at first then everything suddenly fall apart and became so much brighter than it was before.<br><br>It <b>started very confusing</b>. A little bit too unimaginable. Teri Terry didn't describe things in details. Some parts was left me to judge how. As it has "future-background", I think I'm not the only one that have a right to get the background in details. How was the city? How was the hospital? How was the house that Kyla lives? How was everything in landscape around? It was never told in details. <i>THAT's what very disappointing.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465541365ra/19370379.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

I finally knew what <pre> LEVO </pre> is, what <pre> ABOLISHED </pre> means and how it impact to lives, and so many else about things that didn't there in real life today. But overall, <b>the plot was terrific</b>. It has fast pace. It is told in flow. I never lost the time what was happened. Chapters had a few pages to tell me scene by scenes. I remember the <pre> DRAGON-MOM </pre> that started as a difficult mom then ended as a caring and understanding mom. <br><br>But for me, there people that hard to understand. I don't know exactly who or what is Kyla's father. Some parts he's so gentle I almost like this man. Then other parts, he's so cruel and ridiculous. Everything about him left me guessing. People like Sister Penny, the Doctor (I forgot his name, sorry), and so many many more. I don't even know their role here. Are they the good men or the bad men? <br><br><blockquote>

She's like a diamond hidden inside her soul. I love her and clueless face as described. For Ben, I don't know. I cannot guess. He's stupid (?). Well, let's see. If he appeared in second book, I'll manage to judge him again. If not, BYE, I thought he's stupid.<br><br><blockquote>

Let's see how it will end. But when I love the prequel, I gave too much expectation for the next. Hope it won't let me down. *finger-crossed*<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_951735220" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/951735220" />
    <a title="Hannah " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3431708-hannah"><img alt="Hannah " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508180952p2/3431708.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/951735220?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah " href="/user/show/3431708-hannah">Hannah </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3431708-hannah?shelf=2016-oct-2017-oct">2016-oct-2017-oct</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3431708-hannah?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3431708-hannah?shelf=dropped-series">dropped-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer951735220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13190284972039624884"><a href='www.psilovethatbook.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>@ P.S. I love that book!</a><br/><br/>EXPECTATIONS: I think I saw this book in the library first time. Since then I have taken it and given it back without reading at least twice so eventually when I got an audiobook I decided that it is time I finally get to it.<br/><br/>THE WORLD: I would say it is similar to our world and at the same time not exactly. We do have a human society but there is also a much advanced technology present than in our world. Basically if you do something horrible and are underage you are not </span>
  <span id="freeText13190284972039624884" style="display:none"><a href="www.psilovethatbook.com" rel="nofollow noopener">@ P.S. I love that book!</a><br /><br />EXPECTATIONS: I think I saw this book in the library first time. Since then I have taken it and given it back without reading at least twice so eventually when I got an audiobook I decided that it is time I finally get to it.<br /><br />THE WORLD: I would say it is similar to our world and at the same time not exactly. We do have a human society but there is also a much advanced technology present than in our world. Basically if you do something horrible and are underage you are not put in prison but instead your memory is wiped out aka slated. You are giving new identity and a new chance. Basically if you are slated a family will take you in, you will go to school and such as normal but you have this device attached to you that monitors your violence levels. So if you decide to do something violent again it will knock you out. And then eventually when you reach certain age you are asked if you want to go on living without your memories or if you want to know why you were slated. Pretty simple concept I think.<br /><br />CHARACTERS: Our main character is called Kyla and she has been freshly slated at the beginning of the book. She is placed in a family which already is raising a slated girl and life really goes on without a big changes. However, Kyla has these panic attacks that elevate her levels which dangerous so she is forbidden to do much outside school. Also in school we meet other slated people who eventually start forming a group of course. However, it is not so open as you might thing. The government is kinda wiping out supposed enemies too so what Kyla and her friends do has to be in secret. Okay so let's talk about Kyla's personality. Well not really much to it, she is pretty calm maybe even too calm for this book tbh. As a reader I didn't really have any feelings towards her. I do know who she is but it's a bit so so when I think of her. And then her friends...I am not sure if they are really characters or just props for Kyla. Let's just say that this book was more about the secrets and politics of government than about character development.<br /><br />ROMANCE: Not really a center of this book. There is attachment and some shocking twists but this book is not about romance. Which of course is very refreshing when it comes to dystopian books, so point there Teri Terry!<br /><br />GOOD: Even it is so not new I still liked the idea of memory swiping. I think it makes more sense than just to shut people in prison for years.<br /><br />BAD: It was predictable and not very unique. I mean okay when it comes to dystopian book I guess nothing is really unique anymore but still, it felt like the author wasn't even really trying to do something new. Shame.<br /><br />OVERALL: It was on a good side of okay I guess. If I read this book back in days when I was reading a lot of dystopian I probably would have loved it. As of today, it was an interesting few hours I spent listening to it but I will not continue with the series.<br /><br /><a href="www.psilovethatbook.com" rel="nofollow noopener">@ P.S. I love that book!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13190284972039624884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_280475439" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/280475439" />
    <a title="Emily Blake" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5242354-emily-blake"><img alt="Emily Blake" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514927963p2/5242354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/280475439?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily Blake" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily Blake" href="/user/show/5242354-emily-blake">Emily Blake</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5242354-emily-blake?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5242354-emily-blake?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5242354-emily-blake?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5242354-emily-blake?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5242354-emily-blake?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5242354-emily-blake?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5242354-emily-blake?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5242354-emily-blake?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer280475439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8106905708613310691">*<b>An ARC was provided by Orchard Books in exchange for an honest review</b>*<br/><br/>After reading all the rave reviews about this book I was super excited to get the chance to read it. And it didn’t disappoint.<br/><br/>First off, may I just say that this is one of the most original, imaginative ideas I have seen in a book in a long time. I have a friend who has diabetes, so I think that Terry got the idea for the Levos from that, but it was such an interesting spin on it that I honestly didn’t care. Everything about </span>
  <span id="freeText8106905708613310691" style="display:none">*<b>An ARC was provided by Orchard Books in exchange for an honest review</b>*<br /><br />After reading all the rave reviews about this book I was super excited to get the chance to read it. And it didn’t disappoint.<br /><br />First off, may I just say that this is one of the most original, imaginative ideas I have seen in a book in a long time. I have a friend who has diabetes, so I think that Terry got the idea for the Levos from that, but it was such an interesting spin on it that I honestly didn’t care. Everything about this book I loved: the writing, the story line, and the staging. Everything worked it’s way up to an amazing climax, with all the events flowing together perfectly and amazing, amazing writing finishing it all off.<br /><br />One thing that I really liked about this book and have not seen in any book I’ve read before is the romance, or lack there of. I loved that Ben and Kyla were friends and not together because it would have messed it up. I think the fact that they were best friends and then started having feelings for each other was a much better way to convey the romance and you really feel it more.<br />It also helped because it made Kyla, who was already a very strong character, seem even stronger.<br />And Ben was different too. In most books the main boy character is super hot, sexy, all that, but Ben wasn’t, and I love that. He was a normal guy, and that made the friendship and romance that much more believable.<br /><br />Wow Terry, just wow. You have penned a masterpiece of a debut novel. I honestly don’t think I have read a debut novel this good before.<br /><br /><br />~Emily @ <a href="http://emilyscrammedbookshelf.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Emily's Crammed Bookshelf</a></span>

          </span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_49477216'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49477216-falling-skye---kannst-du-deinem-verstand-trauen"><img alt="Falling Skye - Kannst du deinem Verstand trauen? (Falling Skye, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1586851341l/49477216._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qfGtLtHwlqBMsPjXjTuKhn4Uqh9WoHtLyyXq8/YFz+aT18T8aq5fyOubTLZ6zoBZqEtN15gt9SyQW6xCO0Y9fA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6eWtmIBPH9JgZBtZ37Alwvip3L2AC5bibN6ThHKwBLLTw8RKOxHWusdPrzgoRS8dLvY7dU6GGIU3oNU1v/P2KA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer1219652144937784386">Teri has lived in France, Canada, Australia and England at more addresses than she can count, acquiring three degrees, a selection of passports and a silly name along the way.   <span id="freeText1219652144937784386" style="display:none">Teri has lived in France, Canada, Australia and England at more addresses than she can count, acquiring three degrees, a selection of passports and a silly name along the way. Past careers have included scientist, lawyer, optometrist, and, in England, various jobs in schools, libraries and an audiobook charity. The footpaths and canal ways of the Buckinghamshire Chilterns where she now lives inspired much of the setting of Slated. She hates broccoli, likes cats, and has finally worked out what she wants to do when she grows up.<br /><br />Facebook fan page: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/TeriTerryAuthor">http://www.facebook.com/TeriTerryAuthor</a><br />Notes from the Slushpile: group blog on writing for children <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://notesfromtheslushpile.blogspot.co.uk/">http://notesfromtheslushpile.blogspot...</a><br /><br />**IMPORTANT: Please do not message me on Goodreads with requests for review copies, swag, interviews, or anything else. See the contact section of my website for that. Messages on Goodreads may (and probably will) go unanswered!**</span>
